SUBENT        14854001   20250815                             152414854001    1 
BIB                 13         70                                 14854001    2 
TITLE      Prompt-fission neutron spectra in the 235U(n,f)        14854001    3 
           reaction                                               14854001    4 
AUTHOR     (B.Mauss,J.Taieb,B.Laurent,G.Belier,A.Chatillon,       14854001    5 
           D.Etasse,P.Morfouace,O.Roig,M.Devlin,R.C.Haight,       14854001    6 
           K.J.Kelly)                                             14854001    7 
REFERENCE  (J,PR/C,111,044611,2025)                               14854001    8 
           #doi:10.1103/PhysRevC.111.044611                       14854001    9 
REL-REF    (M,14684001,P.Marini+,J,PR/C,101,044614,2020) The      14854001   10 
           experimental method and the analysis.                  14854001   11 
INSTITUTE  (2FR BRC,2FR SAC,2FR CAE,1USALAS)                      14854001   12 
FACILITY   (LINAC,1USALAS) Weapon Neutron Research (WNR)          14854001   13 
           facility of the Los Alamos Neutron Science Center      14854001   14 
            (LANSCE).                                             14854001   15 
INC-SOURCE (SPALL) The LANSCE linear accelerator provided a       14854001   16 
           pulsed beam of 800 MeV protons impinging on a          14854001   17 
           tungsten target at WNR. Spallation reactions were      14854001   18 
           generated and produced a white neutron source, with    14854001   19 
           neutron energies ranging from below 1 MeV to about     14854001   20 
           700 MeV.                                               14854001   21 
DETECTOR   (FISCH,SCIN) The setup was formed of a fission         14854001   22 
           chamber containing 22 235U samples, surrounded by the  14854001   23 
           54 liquid scintillators of the Chi-Nu array, placed 1  14854001   24 
           m away from the target position. The chamber was       14854001   25 
           filled with high-purity CF4 gas and operated at a      14854001   26 
           fixed pressure of about 900 mbar, 100 mbar above the   14854001   27 
           local atmospheric pressure. It allowed for the use of  14854001   28 
           thin structural material, thereby minimizing the       14854001   29 
           parasitic scattering of incoming and fission neutrons. 14854001   30 
SAMPLE     22 samples of 2.5 mg of uranium 235 were each          14854001   31 
           deposited on an aluminum backing within a 33 mm        14854001   32 
           diameter circle at the European Commission Joint       14854001   33 
           Research Center of Geel, Belgium. The 22 samples had   14854001   34 
           an isotopic purity above 99.9% and amount to a total   14854001   35 
           of 55 mg of radioactive material used as target for    14854001   36 
           the incident neutrons. The multiplate fission chamber  14854001   37 
           contained the stack of 22 samples, with their backing  14854001   38 
           serving as cathodes, and 11 anodes, assembled on       14854001   39 
           three insulating rods.                                 14854001   40 
METHOD     (TOF) The double time of flight (ToF) method was used  14854001   41 
           to measure the incoming and prompt fission neutrons    14854001   42 
           energies. The detection of fission fragments inside    14854001   43 
           the fission chamber provided a reference time for      14854001   44 
           fission events. It was compared to the time of the     14854001   45 
           proton pulse, T0, which provided an effective neutron  14854001   46 
           time resolution of 0.5 ns or less, to determine the    14854001   47 
           ToF of the incoming neutron. Incoming neutron          14854001   48 
           energies were extracted event by event from the        14854001   49 
           length of the flight path and the measured ToF.        14854001   50 
           Following the fission event, the prompt fission        14854001   51 
           neutrons were detected in the liquid scintillators     14854001   52 
           forming the Chi-Nu array. Prompt fission neutron       14854001   53 
           energies were extracted from the ToF between the       14854001   54 
           fission chamber and the Chi-Nu detectors. The          14854001   55 
           experimental setup was placed on the 15 degree left    14854001   56 
           flight path (4FP15L), at 21.5 m from the production    14854001   57 
           target.                                                14854001   58 
CORRECTION The so-called wraparound correction was needed         14854001   59 
           because of the pulsed structure of the beam. Beam      14854001   60 
           leakage current correction was needed because of an    14854001   61 
           issue with the LANSCE proton accelerator. Additional   14854001   62 
           corrections to the mean energy: to calculate the mean  14854001   63 
           energy over the full range of the actual PFNS, the     14854001   64 
           measured PFNS had to be extrapolated over the low      14854001   65 
           energy range. The simulated measurement of 235U(n,f)   14854001   66 
           spectra at each incoming neutron energy were           14854001   67 
           corrected for the intrinsic efficiency calculated      14854001   68 
           using the 252Cf(sf) simulated measurement, and         14854001   69 
           extrapolated to lower energies.                        14854001   70
